Tense Situation in Estonia 41

Guomin, Reval, 14th - The situation in Estonia is becoming increasingly dangerous. After the government declared a state of emergency in the country, it disbanded various military organizations today, including the headquarters of the Estonian Freedom Fighters, who support National Socialism, and restricted public gatherings, meetings, and freedom of speech in newspapers. Political observers say that this plan may not be effective, because the Freedom Fighters have already gained the support of the majority of the people.

Reval: The Estonian government has decided to build two submarines and several new torpedo boats in the near future. The government recently sold two torpedo cruisers to the Peruvian government for 4.1 million yuan, which is not enough to cover the cost of the new ships. Therefore, it plans to raise another public bond to make up for the shortfall. (Guomin dispatch, 14th)

Opening of the Fifth Pan-Pacific Academic Conference

Soviet Russia Did Not Send Representatives to Participate 42

Maritime Arms, Tariffs, etc. are Major Issues

Efforts to Avoid Detailed Discussion of Chinese-Japanese Disputes

Hu Shi's Speech Condemns Various Countries' Competition in Naval Armaments

British and Japanese Representatives Speak Against Each Other on Trade War

The Pan-Pacific Academic Conference opened here today. Judging from the current situation, the conference seems likely to be uneventful, unless some representatives only want to discuss the more contentious issues affecting the Far East. Canadian representative Falconer welcomed the representatives at the opening ceremony, saying that the Pacific countries should strive to establish a friendship similar to that between the United States and Canada. He believed that this conference would help to realize this friendship. Judging from the conversations in the lounge, it seems that the leaders of the conference have tried to create an agenda that will not provoke fierce debates. According to some representatives, the relations between China and Japan are enough to cause intense disputes, so some issues will be avoided if possible. If unlimited debates are conducted on the Far Eastern issue in some areas, it may endanger the life of the conference. The status of Soviet Russia in the Far East may also not be discussed in detail, because Canadian law prohibits communists from entering the country, and Soviet Russia has not sent a representative to the conference. Even the Manchurian issue, although some representatives have tried to raise it, may not be discussed in detail, and the outcome is unknown. (Guomin dispatch, 14th)

The Fifth Pan-Pacific Academic Conference was held here today. The issues discussed include maritime arms in the Pacific, restrictions on tariffs and trade, agreements on international commodities, shipping subsidies, Philippine independence, and the US law prohibiting the entry of Easterners. Representatives from countries related to the Pacific are attending. Sir Wilton, a non-official member of the Hong Kong Legislative Council, and Mr. Woodhead, an Englishman from Shanghai, also came to participate. Chairman Falconer expressed his confidence that the work of the conference would be successful today, and spoke about the relationship between Canada and the United States, saying that if someone attacked Canada, the result would be that the United States would join Canada's side and take action if a non-British person gained a position in Canada. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

Pengfu: Chinese representative Hu Shi spoke at the opening day of the Pan-Pacific Academic Conference, condemning the various countries' competition in naval armaments. He said that the ship-building plans that the United States has implemented and is negotiating with various countries are bound to destroy the peace machinery that has been built with hard work for decades. A few years ago, countries strongly urged the dismantling of war tools, but now they have turned to dismantling peace tools, which is regrettable. Japanese representative Nitobe spoke, strongly stating that the economic war is intensifying, and the danger is worrying. It is necessary to have a reasonable adjustment between countries, implicitly referring to the increased tariffs on non-British goods in British colonies and the US economic plan. British representative, former High Commissioner of Palestine, Samuel, claimed that Britain, in the Far East, apart from maintaining its original trade, only wants to promote the security of the region. Britain does not want to obtain special interests, especially not interfering. (Guomin dispatch, 15th)

Oriental Immigrants Should Receive Equal Treatment 43

California Chamber of Commerce Passes Resolution

Reversing Previous Stance

San Francisco: The California Chamber of Commerce in the United States passed a resolution today advocating that the US Congress repeal the clauses in the immigration law that reject Eastern nationalities, and give Eastern nationalities the same immigration quota. Because California has always been the strongest opponent of Eastern nationalities immigrating to the United States, this time, the state Chamber of Commerce organized a special committee to conduct a detailed study of this issue from all aspects, and made a resolution in favor, which can greatly promote the newly emerging movement to allow Eastern immigrants. According to the Chamber of Commerce directors, if the Eastern nationalities are given immigration quotas according to current laws, Japanese people can immigrate to the United States at a rate of 185 people per year, and Chinese people can immigrate at a rate of 105 people per year. This small matter will not have harmful consequences for the labor community, and its impact will be sufficient to improve international relations and increase trade. The current movement has spread to the Atlantic coast of the United States. (Guomin News Agency dispatch, 14th)

Pittman Visits Roosevelt

Reports on the Formation of the Silver Agreement 44

It is Expected that Congress Will Approve the Increase in Silver Prices

Highly Praises China and Mexico for Abandoning Selfish Interests as Commendable

Guomin, Washington, 13th - US Senator Pittman met with the President to report on the situation of silver discussions at the World Economic Conference. After leaving the White House, he met with reporters and claimed that the price of silver would eventually return to 60 cents per ounce. It is expected that the United States will pass the silver agreement concluded at the Economic Conference in January next year. Pittman believes that the price of silver can be increased through various activities, and even relying solely on the federal government's purchases, it can rise. Currently, 66 countries have approved the silver plan, and signed the silver resolution, opposing the destruction of silver coins and supporting the promotion of the monetary use of silver. He expects that the countries signing the silver agreement will begin purchasing silver at the beginning of next year, and believes that these signatory countries will soon use some silver as currency collateral. If all countries pay as much attention to raising the price of silver as they do to raising commodity prices, silver will definitely return to its previous price. He also said that the United States' future export trade will mainly focus on the Far East and South America, both of which widely use silver, so the increase in the price of silver may be more beneficial to the United States than to other countries. The Economic Conference was able to pass the silver proposal and conclude a five-nation agreement thanks to the cooperation of Chinese Finance Minister Song Ziwen and Mexican Finance Minister Bani. All the representatives recognized their views on the silver issue as correct and sound. They did not make any demands for the selfish interests of one country, and strived to achieve universal agreement and seek the welfare of the world. Such facts as China's sacrifice of the right to sell silver and Mexico's purchase of silver are all commendable. Mexican Finance Minister Bani also returned home after attending the London meeting, and after arriving in Washington today, he also shared the same views on the price of silver as Pittman.

German Anti-Austrian Conspiracy 70

Austrian Newspaper Publishes Special Edition

Revealing the Inside Story of Activities

(Reuters, Vienna, 14th) Today, the government organ [Federal Post] published a special edition containing detailed plans devised by the German National Socialist Party to subdue Austria and seize Austrian industry and commerce, with a headline in extremely large characters reading, [Conspiracy Against Austria]. According to the newspaper, this plan was discovered in mail being inspected, proving that Germany is currently using the German Embassy in Vienna to illegally transmit information. The most noteworthy document contained therein is a memorandum from German Baron Sigler, advocating granting Austria commercial benefits to win the favor of Austrians. It is said that imposing a forced peace on a conquered Austria is inconceivable. This would only arouse Austrian patriotism, and Germany may not be able to win a war in the new era. Therefore, instead of Germany swallowing up Austrian industries that have become Frenchified and Westernized, they should be enticed with the hope of prosperity through German trade.

(Havas, Vienna, 15th) Yesterday, the semi-official mouthpiece [Federal Post] published various documents proving that the German Embassy in Austria is responsible for relaying messages for the Austrian National Socialist Party. The newspaper believes that this fact, along with the German flights into Austrian territory to distribute leaflets and the use of radio to broadcast propaganda attacking the Austrian government, is of the same nature, proving that Germany continues to carry out movements to disrupt Austrian security. It demanded that the Austrian government determine its position on this matter. The socialist mouthpiece Labor Daily even asked the government to demand that Germany recall its ambassador.

(Havas, Vienna, 15th) Yesterday, Knos, leader of the Austrian National Socialist Party in the Styria province, delivered a radio broadcast speech in the German city of Seng, attacking the Dollfuss government. A phonograph record of the speech was made, and today the German Presslau radio station rebroadcast Knos's speech. Austrian public opinion was extremely indignant at the content of the speech.

(Havas, Vienna, 14th) It has been widely rumored that secret envoys from various German and Austrian factions are conducting negotiations to ease relations between the two countries. However, according to responsible sources, this news is unreliable, as the Austrian government has not been informed of this matter, and no individual official has been authorized to participate in these negotiations.

Germany Arrests Swiss Workers 71

Issue of Sovereignty Over Small Island Arises

(Reuters, Geneva, 14th) Last week, members of the German National Socialist Party crossed into Swiss territory in Basel to search for communists. Now, another case has occurred, which Swiss newspapers are paying close attention to. Last night, German customs officials detained two Swiss workers who were camping on a small island in the Rhine River near Basel. It has been verified that the island did not display any signs prohibiting landing, and the sovereignty of the island has not yet been clarified. The Germans claim that it is definitely German territory, so Swiss tourists have no right to land on the island, and they accuse them of being communists, using the island to spread inflammatory writings. Both workers were carrying communist newspapers and have been imprisoned in a German jail. The Swiss authorities are very concerned about this case and are currently investigating it.

This currently affects 12,000 workers, and it is expected that another 5,000 will be unemployed by Wednesday. Russian Government Allocates Funds to Purchase Cattle 73

(Reuters, Moscow, 15th) Soviet Russian Communist Party Secretary General Stalin and People's Commissar Chairman Molotov signed an order allocating 35 million rubles to purchase one million head of cattle to supply to rural farmers. In the future, members of Soviet Russian cooperatives will be allowed to own their own cattle. This move is inconsistent with common communist principles and shows a major concession by the Soviet Russian authorities to cooperative farmers. The farmers are dissatisfied with forced collectivization and would rather kill their cattle for food than donate them to the Soviets.

Yellow River Flood Reaches Western Shandong 76

=Area West of Heze and Cao is a Vast Expanse of Water=

=Kao County Dyke Breach Sends Water to Shandong as Well=

=Northern Shandong Canal Suddenly Surges=

(Jinan Correspondence) The Yellow River has experienced high water flows due to heavy rains in Shaanxi. In the territory of Changyuan County, Hebei Province, there were sudden breaches of multiple mouths on both the north and south banks, each several miles wide, and the floodwaters rushed down. The water on the north bank reached Ermencun today (13th) and will reach Puxian, Shandong Province in one or two days. The officials and people of the county are currently making every effort to prevent and control the flood. The water exiting on the south bank flowed into Heze in western Shandong yesterday, causing alarming news to spread and stirring up unrest. The natives of Cao Prefecture living in Jinan are particularly anxious due to the immediate suffering. Telegrams and letters of inquiry are pouring in like snowflakes. This is truly a natural disaster that has rarely occurred in Shandong in recent years. According to the River Affairs Bureau today (13th), a telegram report from Heze County Magistrate Sun Zerang stated that the Yellow River water entering Shandong had reached west of Heze, dividing into two streams. One stream flows northwest from Guanyuanji towards Wudian north of the city, and the other stream passes Weilu through Gaozhuangji, also heading towards Wudian, merging into one. The water entering Cao County has also reached the Weiwan area on the western border of Cao County, also dividing into two streams, one towards the south of Cao County City, and the other towards the north of Cao County City. The water situation is unclear. In addition, the upstream general section chief Chen Tianmo and others also telegraphed that the south bank of the Yellow River dyke at Yanmiao, about eight li from Kao County, Henan Province, also breached on the 11th, with a width of several tens of meters, and the flow was turbulent. The southern part of Heze and the northern part of Cao County in Shandong Province are both disaster areas. The following is a record of each report: 1. Sun Zerang's telegram stated, "On the morning of the 1st, the water head had reached the western border of Heze, dividing into two streams. One stream flows northwest from Guanyuanji towards Wudian north of the city, and the other stream passes Weilu through Gaozhuangji towards Wudian. I have been working hard for days, together with the principals of various rural schools and the students of the self-defense teams, to help the villagers protect the dangerous works at Liuzhuang and Zhukou, and at the same time desperately repairing and blocking the dykes on both sides of the waterways, so that the water flow can be discharged. According to reconnaissance reports, the water from Cao County has also reached the Weiwan area on the western border of Cao County, also dividing into two streams, one towards the south of Cao County City, and the other towards the north of Cao County City. The water situation is unclear. Heze County Magistrate Sun Zerang kowtows." 2. Chen Wenmo's telegram stated, "According to a telephone report from Erfenzhuang in Hebei, the dyke on the south bank of Yanmiao, about eight li downstream from Kaocheng, Henan Province, breached on the Zhen day, with a width of about several tens of meters, and the flow was very turbulent. The southern part of Heze and the northern part of Cao County in this province are all disaster areas," etc. Based on this, it is appropriate to report it by telegram. Chen Wenmo, Zhao Rongfu, kowtow.

The Yellow River's major flooding this year first submerged Shaanxi and Shanxi, and recently has affected Hebei, Henan, and Shandong provinces. The counties in western Shandong, such as Heze, are busy with prevention and control, and the northern Shandong Canal has also suddenly surged. Today (13th), the Shandong Civil Affairs Department received a report from the De County Magistrate stating that the water level suddenly rose by more than three feet last night, leaving only four feet before reaching the top of the dyke, and the situation is extremely dangerous. They are currently supervising the militia to work together to prevent and control the flood. After receiving the telegram, Civil Affairs Director Li Shuchun reported it to the provincial government and notified the Construction Department, and at the same time telegraphed the county magistrate to do his best to defend. (13th)

Chongming Seawall in Danger 77

=The Vortex in Front of Qinglong Dam is Forty-Five Meters Deep=

=Local Groups Have Sent Representatives to the Province to Petition=

Chongming is located at the mouth of the Yangtze River, surrounded by the sea on all sides, and is the throat of the Yangtze River and an important place for coastal defense. During the Qing Dynasty, it was where the Su, Song, and Chang General Zhen was stationed, with forts built in its subordinate towns and fortresses. It was abolished after the reforms. In the past, the British went to investigate and were willing to exchange it for Weihaiwei. When the January 28th Incident occurred, more than twenty Japanese warships were moored along its southern coast (ie, Liuhe Baimao Port), and they even landed in the county to buy goods, so there was a rumor that it had been lost. The island was established as a county during the Song Dynasty, but due to the erosion of the river, it has collapsed and expanded frequently, and the county government has been moved five times. During the reign of Emperor Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, in the 20th and 26th years, local people successively requested funds to build a stone seawall more than a thousand zhang long south of the city, and the people donated 5,000 mu of sandy land, named Seawall Public Land, as the annual repair fund for the wall. It has been safe for more than thirty years. In the 17th year of the Republic, Waisha County (ie, today's Qidong) was split off from the county. As a result, all public property was divided item by item. There was a dispute over the aforementioned seawall public land. Later, the Jiangsu Provincial Government mediated, and the Finance Department subsidized Chongming and Qidong counties each with 5,000 yuan per year, and the fields were divided equally. Although the case was decided, it has not been implemented to date. Last year, people from Chongming and Qidong counties requested to merge, but the case was shelved by the provincial government. Recently, the No. 2 seawall south of the county town is extremely dangerous. The Construction Department sent a guiding engineer to measure it. The vortex in front of the Qinglong Dam is forty-five meters deep, and the width is almost a mile. The stone embankment has collapsed more than twenty zhang. The estimated repair project will cost more than 100,000 yuan, causing public panic. The county party department took the lead in sending a telegram to the province requesting relief. Various groups such as the County Farmers' Association and local gentry Wang Qingmu, Zhu Songhan, etc., jointly submitted a petition to the province requesting the issuance of outstanding subsidies and the seawall public rent divided by Qidong County to repair it, and sent Cheng Tiuyun, a member of the County Executive Committee, and Tao Zhu, director of the Property Office, to the province to petition the provincial government and the two departments of finance and construction. During the great flood this month, another three zhang of the stone embankment collapsed, and pedestrians are now detouring.

End of Songjiang Constitution Research Association 78

The Jiangsu Provincial Constitution Research Association sent a copy of the draft constitution and a copy of Zhang Zhiben's "Opinions on the Constitution" to this county, instructing it to organize a Songjiang branch in accordance with regulations, engage in research, and strive to collect wisdom from various sources. County Magistrate Jin, in accordance with the regulations, in addition to appointing representatives from various legal organizations and county party departments, as well as leaders from various courts, bureaus, and sections as members, also specially invited erudite scholars Lu Longxiang, Ni Guangrong, Chen Qiushi, Shen Lianbi, Jiang Xuezhu, and Peng Weiji, a total of six people, to be members. He convened a meeting to distribute the draft constitution and reference opinions, printed and sent to each member, who annotated their opinions on each article. These were then submitted for review and approval. Today (the 15th) at 1:00 PM, the county government convened another meeting to compile and read aloud the opinions annotated by each member, discussing them article by article. After passing them, they will be submitted to the Provincial Research Association. The county's research association will then conclude its work.

Suzhou Supervisory Committee Member Gao Yihan Arrives in Suzhou 79

Supervisory Committee Member Gao Yihan arrived in Suzhou on the 14th and stayed at the Garden Hotel. On the morning of the 15th at 10:00 AM, he went to the High Court to investigate the judicial situation, then inspected the District Court. In the afternoon, he went to the County Government to give a lecture to the staff of various sections. On the 16th, he went to Wujiang for inspection, and then went to Baoshan, Taicang, and other places to inspect the seawall projects.

Handover Between Old and New Members of Wuxi Municipal Management Committee 80

The new members of the Wuxi Municipal Property Management Committee, including Gu Shuzhi and five others, were officially appointed by the province and took office on the 10th of this month. Yesterday was the day for the handover between the old and new members. The former committee chairman, Qian Sunqing, handed over all vouchers, books, instruments, annual reports, account books, files, agendas, various business license donations, silver, seals, and other items to the new committee chairman, Gu Shuzhi, according to the records. After the handover was completed, Gu convened a meeting of the staff and gave a speech, mainly urging all staff to work hard and serve the public. In the future, the donation matters must be rectified to fulfill the responsibilities.

Establishing a Reformatory to Deal with Vagrants 81

The county government convened its 198th county administration meeting on the morning before yesterday. Chairman was County Magistrate Yan. The meeting resolved: (1) In accordance with the instructions of the Second District Commissioner's Office, a portion of the buildings of the Civilian Vocational Training Center will be separated to establish a reformatory for the purpose of dealing with local ruffians and vagrants who cause harm to the area, sending them to the reformatory for reformation at any time. The reformatory affairs will be concurrently managed by Director Wu of the Vocational Training Center. The expenses will be appropriated by the county from the local fees. (2) In accordance with the provincial order, radio receivers will be installed, and students will be sent to the Radio Operator Training Class of the Central Broadcasting Station Administration. However, the expenses should be allocated from the industrial fees after being approved by the Construction Department before students are sent. The rest is omitted.

Various Districts of Changzhou Report Famine 82

Since the beginning of summer, there has been little rain in Wu County. Although the crops have been irrigated several times, it has been of no avail. The ditches and streams are about to dry up, forming a famine situation. The county government has received successive reports of famine from the heads of the 10th, 12th, 18th, and 19th districts. Yesterday, it instructed them to investigate the details of the famine-stricken fields, compile a register, and submit it for further investigation.

Changshu Villages Joyfully Receive Rain 83

Since the beginning of summer, there has been no rain for a long time. The drought in various villages has had a great impact on agricultural crops. Cotton and rice are showing signs of withering, and farmers are worried. The authorities in various villages have successively reported disasters. Therefore, all villages have offered sacrifices to the Dragon King to pray for rain, and there have been proposals to hold Dragon King festivals. The authorities could not prohibit it. The day before yesterday afternoon, the air suddenly changed, with dense rain clouds, flashing lightning, and strong cool winds. Immediately, there was a heavy rainstorm, and water accumulated into channels in an instant. However, the soil had been cracked for a long time, and it was still not enough. That night, there was another torrential rain, which greatly moistened the fields and rice. The next morning, farmers gathered at tea houses and celebrated the rainfall of the previous day.

Doubts Arise After Autopsy in Jiangyin Changshou Murder Case 84

Jin Yuan, the son of Chen Rurong of West Street, Changshou Township, 9th District, was strangled to death by his wife, Jiang Acui, and her lover, He Aqi. The case was reported to the county for an autopsy. The autopsy officer, Cao Mingde, based on the old method of "Xiyuan Records," found rope marks on the deceased's neck that were "crossed in an eight," and concluded that it was suicide. The chest wounds were said to be caused by the deceased hitting himself after hanging. The audience at the time was very indignant. Fortunately, Trial Officer Shi handled the matter properly, and the situation was calmed. Now, the entire town is still very angry, and a public petition has been submitted to the county government, raising six doubts to vindicate the deceased.

Zhenjiang Flood Control Engineering Office Merged 85

The First District General Engineering Office of the Yangtze River Flood Control Commission has been established for a month. For the convenience of office work, the office was attached to the Mechanical Section of the Construction Department on the second floor. Now that the Yangtze River floods are no longer a problem, various offices are being closed one after another. All engineers and staff of the First District General Engineering Office were originally concurrently serving as full-time staff of the Yangtze River Survey Team. Now that the task is about to be completed, the General Engineering Office will be merged into the office of the team on Jiangbian Second Road in this port starting today.

Nantong Japanese Woman Kills Husband and Refuses Interrogation 86

Huang Yulun, a professor of medicine at Nantong University, accused his Japanese wife, Otsuka Kaneko, of murder. The procuratorate summoned her on the 14th, but the Japanese woman refused to appear, saying that she was a Japanese national and not subject to Chinese court trials. The court has requested the High Court to review and instruct on how to handle the matter.

Surveying and Measurement of Huainan Salt Land Begins 87

The Ministry of Finance is reorganizing the Huainan salt land in order to facilitate the division for reclamation. It has specially appointed Wang Zhaohua as the director of the Huainan salt land survey, starting from Jinsha in Tongzhou and ending in Gaoning. The surveying and measurement began on the 15th.

Riot at Nursing Home Subsides 88

The riot at the Nantong Nursing Home, where the elderly opposed the director Ma Boxian, has now subsided. The Charity Management Office has decided to thoroughly reform the nursing home and has appointed Yuan Jianhou as the new director.

Water Level in Qingjiang Canal Continues to Rise by Seven Inches 89

Recently, the water level in the canal has been rising and falling repeatedly. Yesterday (the 12th), the water level rose by another seven inches. Together with the three inches that rose the day before yesterday, it has risen by a foot in total. The water level in the Qingjiang Sluice Gate was originally 2 zhang, 3 chi, and 9 cun, but it has now risen to 2 zhang, 4 chi, and 9 cun. Those involved in river affairs here said that the rise in water this time mostly comes from Shandong, which is commonly known as the Yi River. If the weather can clear up, even if it is the Yi River, there will not be any danger.

Pinghu Gang of Smugglers Resist Arrest and Seize Weapons 90

The Jin Si Niang Bridge in this county has always been an area where bandits appear. The day before yesterday, a large number of smuggling boats were exporting goods. The tax police stationed in the area learned of this and dispatched a squad led by squad leader Li to pursue them. The smugglers, seeing that the police force was small, resisted. The two sides exchanged fire for about an hour. Li's squad was defeated and returned, and five rifles were lost. The batch of smuggling boats then escaped. Afterwards, Li telegraphed the Liang Yuanhua district squad. District Captain Huang received the report and drove to Zha Pu yesterday, mobilizing all the officers and soldiers of the 6th Detachment of the Zha Pu tax police to pursue them. They caught one smuggling boat, and the five rifles that had been seized were also inside the boat, so they towed it back and reprimanded Squad Leader Li, ordering him to find out the origins of the smuggling gang in order to suppress them.

Major Suspect Arrested in Hangzhou Kidnapping and Murder Case 91

After the kidnapping of Sun Hongwen, the three-year-old son of Sun Xijun, the owner of the Qian Yuan Sugar Shop at No. 32 Longshezui, Jiang Qianxiang in this city, and the shooting of the car driver Qian Jingchun on Wansongling, the military and police agencies immediately dispatched a large number of military and police to investigate and arrest the perpetrators separately. From today (15th), a search of the mountains will be carried out. Unexpectedly, at about 5:00 AM this morning, Inspector Kong Yuesheng of the First Branch Bureau led a number of police officers to search Wugong Mountain and arrested Cao Youcheng, a suspect who was considered to be extremely important, in the Wugong Temple. Because he spoke evasively, the suspect was taken to the First Branch Bureau for questioning. According to his confession, he was from Xinchang, 36 years old, and had served as a senior officer in the Zhenhai Fortress. He came to Hangzhou because of a lawsuit. Later, a note was found beside him, which read: "If the money is not paid by the 13th, people will be beaten and houses will be burned." The accountant of the Zhejiang Fujiang Motor Company and the mother of the hostage went to identify him and confirmed that he was indeed the bandit who hired the car that day. The suspect was wearing a white cloth shirt and was calm. He firmly denied the bandit case and claimed that he was introduced by his friend Song Aquan to stay at the temple. The police were dispatched to No. 42 and No. 30 Baimao Temple Alley to arrest six suspected criminals, including Song Aquan, Song Wangshi, Fang Tingxiu, and Song Qian, both male and female. They are being taken into custody for strict interrogation.

Kidnapping and Robbery Case in Qian'ao Township, Ningbo Yin County 92

On the night of the 11th at 11:30 PM, more than ten pirates suddenly came to the home of Xu Zhengtang, a resident of Qian'ao Township, Jiangshan, Yin County. Xu Zhengtang and his son, Fuxing, who had served as police, escaped through the back door and crossed the river, fortunately avoiding disaster. Only more than 80 silver dollars and a few pieces of jewelry were robbed. After the robbery, the bandits went to the home of Xu Xingchao, a neighbor, to rob again and kidnapped Xu Xingchao, his eleven-year-old son, Shengfu, and his nephew, Zhang Xiaodou. At that time, a hired worker, Yan A Ming, came out to look, and was hacked to death by the bandits.

Gang of Bandits Loot Eight Jiang Camps in Mingguang 93

A gang of bandits of more than 100 people led by Ma Dianwen, who were entrenched in the Sujia Lane area, burned and looted the two villages of Sunying and Nanlu on the 12th. Most of them moved north and sneaked into the Eight Jiang Camps (composed of villages) in the border area of ​​Anhui that night, ambushing in the sorghum fields. When each camp opened its gates at dawn, they took advantage of the situation to enter. Squadron leader Jiang Wenhua led the villagers to resist, but they were eventually defeated. Eight villages fell one after another. After investigation, the villages were almost completely burned down. In addition to looting more than a dozen women and seizing more than 20 guns, many strong men died. The situation was tragic.

Kidnapping Occurs on North Street 94

Li Chuanfa, the owner of the Hua Yu Grain Store on North Street in this port, has a small but comfortable home. He has a son named Kaoshan, who is only eight years old. Yesterday (the 12th) at about 9:00 AM, the family was enjoying the cool in the backyard when three bandits suddenly came. One was with the people outside the door, and two went straight into the backyard, claiming to be looking for something. They wrapped Kaoshan in a sheet and carried him out of the bed. Li was shocked and shouted wildly. The bandits fired a shot and slipped into the alley, exiting the street from the back door. By the time the military and police arrived after hearing the news, the bandits had disappeared without a trace.

Murder Occurs at Baimahu Fish Farm in Xiaoshan 95

Since Dong Xiaohou and others organized the Xingye Fish Farming Cooperative at Baimahu in Xixiang, Xiaoshan, and the fish have been raised under official supervision, all nearby fishermen are not allowed to catch fresh fish in the lake privately. On the 11th of this month, two daughters of a fisherman named Chen from a nearby village were catching shrimp and fish along the lake when they were spotted by the cooperative's managers, who overturned their fishing boat, drowning a thirteen-year-old girl. This aroused the anger of all the fishermen in the village, who called on four to five hundred fishermen to expel the managers of the Xingye Fish Farming Cooperative. On the 12th, five to six hundred fishermen went to the county to appeal and took the girl's body to the county court for an autopsy. A criminal prosecution has been filed.

Early Rice Has Developed Rice Borers 96

There has been more sunshine than rain in Xiaoshan for nearly a month. Since the beginning of autumn, the damage from the fierce sun has increased, and many rice paddies have withered. Now, due to the long period of sunny weather, most of the early rice has developed rice borers, and the rice ears have turned white. After the rice paddies in the southeast have turned white, the general farmers are worried. The county government has sent pest control committees to inspect the villages.

Special Article

Li Zhun's Sea Patrol Diary (Continued) 97

At 11:20 AM, the anchor was dropped, and the anchor chain was almost completely used up. The water there was clear, and in the sunlight, the seabed could be seen. There were many red and white corals, as large as pine and cypress trees. There was a kind of white ribbonfish, about ten feet long, which was intertwined and circled within the coral trees, turning endlessly. After lunch, I led the others to board the shore by sampan. Guoxiang asked me not to sit in a sampan, but to use a larger flat-bottomed boat, so that I could get ashore. I followed his advice. Indeed, I could only reach the shallow beach closest to the shore. Those who took the sampan could not enter. Guoxiang had bought seven or eight of these boats at the harbor. I initially thought they were useless, but now I know they are useful. I still held a wooden stick, left the boat, and stepped over piles of stones to pass. Jumping from this stone to that stone, the distance varied, some were far, some were near, some were high, and some were low. The boat could not move forward, and without this, I could not reach the other shore. I was standing on a large, round stone, wanting to jump again, but the distance was a little far, and I was afraid of falling into the water. I hesitated again and again, and the stone I was standing on moved. I thought it was because of my weight, but the stone had already started to move forward. I was frightened and almost fell. The stone moved closer to the other stone, and then I jumped over. I asked in surprise, "How can the stone move?" Guoxiang and Jingrong said respectfully, "This stone is a giant clam in the sea. Its shell has grown green moss for who knows how many years." I also saw a fish, its color black mixed with red and yellow. Guoxiang said, "This is a small whale, also seven or eight feet long. The tide is receding and it cannot get out, so it is trapped in this shallow water." I poked it with a stick, and water sprayed out of a hole in its head, as high as ten feet. I quickly went ashore and saw many red crabs on the sand, different from other crabs. Their claws were long and numerous, and they moved very fast. When I hit them with a stick, they immediately escaped into a snail shell and disappeared. When I picked up the shell, I saw their claws curled up inside the shell, without any trace. Each crab had a shell, no more than two inches in size. The shell of one crab had been picked up by someone else, so it had nowhere to return, and it curled up on the sand, like a dead thing. I picked up several hundred of them in a bamboo basket to give to friends and relatives, and named them "Hermit Crabs." The workers took shovels ashore and dug in various places and springs, looking for fresh water. After digging more than ten places to a depth of twenty or thirty feet, they could not find any. In fact, it was not an island, but a sandbar.

Westerners also call it "Ailen." This island is no more than six or seven li long, and it takes no more than a few hours to travel around it. There are no large trees on the island. There is a kind of plant that is neither grass nor tree, about ten feet tall and large enough to embrace. The branches and leaves spread out horizontally. Sheltering in this forest is truly a cool world. The sand on the ground is deep black, formed by the accumulation of bird droppings for thousands of years. There are no fierce beasts, insects, or snakes on the island, but there are many birds, mostly gray-black. The large ones raise their heads as tall as a person, with long beaks, and are not afraid of people. When I hit them with a stick, some flew away and some did not. The large ones always fought with people. Instead of defending themselves, they tried to peck at people's eyes. From afar, I saw a large group of birds, about a thousand or more, gathered on the beach. I shot at them three times with a shotgun, but none of them flew away. I thought I had missed, but the guards went to look and found that they had shot down more than thirty birds. The guards chased them away, and they finally flew away, probably because they did not know the power of guns and what humans were. There were many German words carved on the coconut trees and stones, all written in the 1800s. The German, Brown, copied the inscriptions in writing. The stones were not sandstone, but formed by countless coral polyps, so they were named "Coral Stones." Then I came to a place with a stone chamber, eight or nine feet wide, surrounded by coral stones. The top was covered with two extremely large clam shells. I rested here. There was also German carved with knives on the stone, written in 1850. All of them had photos, but I don't know where they were lost after the reform. I ordered the workers to carve words on the coral stone: "[Guangdong Navy Admiral Li Zhun of the Great Qing Dynasty inspected this place in the thirty-third year of Guangxu]." I named it Fubo Island in commemoration of arriving here first on the Fubo. I also ordered the carpenter to make a wooden frame and build a wooden house on the island, covered with coconut palm fronds as walls and paved with coconut palm fronds. A white mast more than five feet high was erected on the side of the house, and the yellow dragon national flag was hung. From then on, this place became Chinese territory. I spent the night on the island. After dusk, I heard a rustling sound in the water. Guoxiang said, "This is a giant sea turtle coming ashore to lay eggs. From now on, we won't have to worry about running out of food." I led the people to each hold an ox-eye lantern, reflecting the light into their chests, and waited on the river. Under the moonlight, I saw large turtles coming up one after another, in countless numbers. We all shone the lights on them, and the turtles immediately retracted their necks and did not move. The sailors inserted wooden sticks under the turtles' bellies and lifted them up with force. They immediately lay on their backs on the sand. There were about twenty of them. Guoxiang said, "That's enough. It's enough food for several hundred of us for three days." Guoxiang also led the sailors to hold bamboo fences and open the accumulated sand under the trees. There were countless turtle eggs, light red in color, round and large like fists. The shell was soft and not hard. We picked up two large baskets. After returning, we scalded them with boiling water, tore open a mouth, and ate them by sucking them. The taste was very good. Guoxiang said, "There are even more bird eggs, but they are not as delicious as turtle eggs." At dawn, I led the people to pick various bird eggs under the trees, of different sizes, some as large as chicken and duck eggs, and some as large as rice bowls, six or seven inches long, all light green in color. The extremely large ones had countless black spots and smelled fishy when cut open. The shell of this extremely large egg was like an ostrich egg, as hard as stone and could not be broken at all. Later, I took it to the provincial capital and asked the ivory carver in Daxin Street to open a skylight and engrave landscapes and figures on it, making it a display item. The giant turtle lying on its back was about ten feet long and six or seven feet wide. The sailors and workers used knives and axes to remove the shell and butcher the meat, and each received a share. The meat was as red as beef, and the skirt was two inches thick. Each turtle yielded twenty or thirty catties, and the total weight was four or five hundred catties. Eight pairs were left, and they were not allowed to be butchered. They were lifted onto the sampan or boat alive and transported to the ship, where they were lifted by a crane. The eight turtles had filled the space in front of the official cabin, so the sailors and workers had no place to rest and eat. So they sat around the turtles' bellies to eat and played cards there. At night, I felt sorry for them lying on their backs and ordered people to turn them over. In the dead of night, the turtles chirped like ducks, making extremely loud noises, causing the people to not be able to sleep. I still ordered the sailors to turn them over on their backs, and they were silent. In the afternoon, I led the people back to the ship, leaving several head of livestock, goats, and water buffalo, male and female, on the island. Brown wept at them, saying, "Alas, these cattle and sheep will die of thirst because there is no fresh water." At noon, we set sail, and after about thirty li, we arrived at another place, with islands on both sides. There was sand on the seabed, where we could anchor, unlike Fubo Island, which was full of coral stones and difficult to anchor. There was sand on the shore, and sampans and boats could all land. Then I led the people to shore. The forests, trees, birds, and everything else were the same as on the previous island. The worker who was digging the well came back after a while and reported that he had found fresh water, and it tasted very good. Digging was only a little over ten feet deep. I tasted it, and it was indeed very sweet. We named it Gan Quan Island and erected a stone monument and raised a flag to commemorate it. This island is about ten or more li long and six or seven li wide. I walked for two or three hours and still could not go around it in a week. On the beach, I picked up something that looked like a golden melon, as large as a tangerine, its color blue-purple. The divisions were interspersed with pearl-white dots, like stone but not stone, light in texture and hollow. There was a stem on top, like a poppy seed capsule, and a hole at the bottom, very beautiful. I don't know what it was. Jingrong said, "This is both animal and plant. If there is a living one, we should find it and show it to the military governor." There were also various other strange and wonderful things that had not been seen in the mainland. There was a stone cup that held cold water without leaking and dried easily. When hot water was put in it, it smelled fishy. It felt like it was made of stone when touched, but its texture was soft. Something that was originally round could be made square or elliptical. Red and white coral were everywhere. The red ones were more than an inch large, but their texture was rough and had few patterns. There were even more white ones. I once picked up a large one, with hundreds of them clustered together, like a mountain shape. I put it in a bauxite box and displayed it in the Jiangnan Industrial Exhibition along with stone gourds and stone tablets. After viewing this island, I also released livestock on it. Then we passed to the island on the other side, which was smaller than Gan Quan Island, no more than eight li long and wide. There was even more coral than before, so we named it Coral Island and erected a stone monument and raised a flag to commemorate it. In the afternoon, we returned to the ship and set sail. After about twenty nautical miles, we arrived at another island. After anchoring, we went ashore by sampan. There was a lot of seaweed in the sea, of unknown length, with small white flowers. The sampan's oars were also blocked by it and could not move forward. We saw a stone with something round like a golden melon on it, with purple flowers blooming on the stem, like butterflies. I said, "This must be the living stone melon that I picked up on the shore yesterday." We anchored the boat close to it, and I personally touched its root, which was about four or five inches long, and seemed to be stony and growing on the stone. I pulled it hard to get it down, and the root broke. White pulp flowed out from under the root, and its smell was very strange, like the meat of crab claws. The flower was very hard and also looked like stone, but it was incomparably bright. I don't know if it was animal or plant. I picked it up and took it back. After a few days, the flowers withered and the pulp inside the shell flowed out, leaving an empty shell, which was presented to Marshal An along with the melon that I picked up earlier and sent to the Jiangnan Industrial Exhibition. After landing and inspecting for a week, the situation was the same as on the other islands. We named it Chenhang Island, erected a stone monument, and raised a flag. We returned to the ship and anchored there that night. On the third day, at dawn, we set sail again. After about ten nautical miles, we arrived at an island. After landing, we saw a fishing boat there, taking hawksbill turtles and raising them in shallow water by the sea, surrounding them with small branches stuck in the water, so they could not leave. I asked the fisherman where he was from.

The fisherman said that he was from Wenchang Lingshui County and came here every year, taking advantage of the clear weather and good wind to come here to take hawksbill turtles, sea cucumbers, and kelp to sell. I asked him how much fresh water and food his boat could hold, and how he dared to take this risk. The fisherman said, "There are only four or five of us. The food is limited, and we can't bring much water. We eat turtle meat, turtle eggs, bird eggs, bird meat, fish, shrimp, and the like. To drink, there are many coconut trees on this island, so we won't die of thirst." I told him that there was an island with fresh water ahead, and if he went there, he wouldn't have to worry about not having fresh water. I looked inside his boat and saw a cabin of large black sea cucumbers and thorn sea cucumbers marinated with lime, all very small. I asked him why he didn't marinate the large black sea cucumbers by the sea, which were more than ten feet long. The fisherman said that the mainland didn't want such large ones. He led me to see the shallow water by the sea, where there was a large black sea cucumber, more than ten feet long, the color of a dead pig. I poked it with a stick, and its meat was like a soft tumor, shedding a piece. Although the skin was very black, the meat was extremely white, but there was no blood. It didn't move much. I thought it was dead. A worker hoeed it with a cross-shaped hoe, shedding another large piece, and the sea cucumber moved forward slightly. It was truly a cold-blooded animal. The situation on the island was the same as on the other islands. After touring around, we named it Linshui Island, erected a stone monument, and raised a clan flag, and went to other islands. All of them were named and had stone monuments erected. One was named Huo Qiu Island, because my sister, Qian Pei, the wife of Grand Prefect Dai Yun, was from Huo Qiu. One was named Gui An Island, because Ding Shao Sun was a native of Gui An. One was named Wucheng Island, because Grand Magistrate Shen Jiwen was from Wucheng. One was named Ningbo Island, because Investigator Li Zichuan was from Ningbo. One was named Xinhui Island, because Sub-Commander Lin Ruijia Guoxiang was from Xinhui. One was named Huayang Island, because Wang Shuwu was from Huayang. One was named Yanghu Island, because Grand Magistrate Liu Ziyi was from Yanghu. One was named Xiuning Island, because Patrol Officer Wu Gaichen Jingrong was from Xiuning. One was named Panyu Island, because Grand Magistrate Wang Zhe Yuan was from Panyu. There was also an island that was further away, about sixty nautical miles, which was twenty or thirty li long. It was formerly named Lincoln, but we renamed it Fengrun Island, in honor of Marshal An, who presided over the great events. Because the sky was changing, we didn't dare to linger any longer, fearing that we would run out of coal and water and not be able to return if the wind rose. On April 23, we sailed away, and after forty-eight hours, we arrived in Hong Kong. The next day, we returned to the province. The trip had taken almost a month. I recounted the whole experience to Marshal An, who was overjoyed and thought that our nautical chart would now include these fourteen Xisha Islands. The strange and wonderful things that we had picked up were displayed in the hall, and colleagues and gentry came to inquire. I was exhausted from explaining and pointing. The islands that we had visited were all drawn into maps by naval surveyors and presented to the Ministry of the Navy and the Army and the Grand Council for record. This expedition, with a very old ship that could not travel more than ten nautical miles and the lives of hundreds of people, was entrusted to Lin Ruijia. It was truly a blessing from heaven, and could not have been achieved solely by human effort. (The End)

Local News

Kong Xiangxi Will Fly to Jiangxi 98

Chairman Chiang Sends Plane to Greet Him

Discussing Financial and Other Issues in Person

Chairman Chiang of the Military Affairs Commission urgently needs to discuss financial and North China issues with Kong Xiangxi, President of the Central Bank. Yesterday, he specially sent his own Sikorsky plane to Shanghai to welcome Kong to Jiangxi. Kong did not depart yesterday due to the suddenness of the matter, but is scheduled to fly to Jiangxi with his entourage this morning to meet with Wang and Chiang. He will stay in Jiangxi for about a week and then return to Shanghai.

Two Ways of Arranging Payment of Debts 99

Kyoto-Shanghai Railway to Pay 270,000 Yuan First

Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway to Discount and Pay 25,000 Pounds

Recently, Western newspapers have repeatedly discussed the overdue principal and interest on the debts of the Kyoto-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou, and Ningbo Railways, especially concerning the Kyoto-Shanghai Railway. However, the railway bureau has not made any statements. According to what was heard yesterday, the bureau has already arranged to pay two batches of principal and interest, which shows that the bureau is earnestly working to reduce its debts and not just giving empty words to evade responsibility. The details of the repayment are recorded below:

The Kyoto-Shanghai Railway has a huge amount of accumulated debt, such as the remaining interest from the 18th to 20th years, the advance payment for purchasing vehicles on behalf of the Sino-British Company, the principal of the maturing loans from the 19th to 22nd years, and the interest on the recent three loans, all of which need to be cleared. Those who pay attention to the affairs of this railway should already know this. Among these overdue payments, one installment of the advance payment for purchasing vehicles, totaling 9,000 British pounds, was repaid within March of this year. The remaining items have not been paid due to a shortage of funds. Now, with active reorganization, 270,000 yuan have been accumulated. It has been decided to allocate all of it to pay off the remaining interest from the 18th year, which is the most overdue. The total amount of this remaining interest is 398,839.20 yuan. After this payment of 270,000 yuan, there will still be 16,839.20 yuan outstanding. It is said that it can also be fully repaid in two months.

The economic situation of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway is slightly better than that of the Kyoto-Shanghai Railway. However, since the Shanghai war last year, the principal of the loan due in May of last year has not been paid on schedule. It has been overdue for several periods, each period being 37,500 pounds. The railway bureau has withdrawn about 200,000 yuan from the special reserve fund of the railway and raised the same amount from the operating cash, totaling 400,000 yuan, which is converted into 25,000 British pounds, and handed over to HSBC to be used as part of the repayment of the principal of the loan due in May of last year. It is said that the remainder will be gradually cleared when a sufficient amount has been accumulated.

American Cotton Resold to Japanese Merchants 104

Tomen Co., Ltd. Has Purchased 4,000 Bales

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, after Finance Minister Song Ziwen established a US$50 million cotton and wheat loan in the United States, the news came that the cotton merchants in Shanghai, both Chinese and foreign, were paying attention to how the American cotton would be sold after it arrived in China. A few days ago, it was rumored that the first batch of American cotton, which was already on its way to China, had been sold by the managers of foreign firms such as Fuga, Anli, and Meian Sanyo. However, these foreign firms immediately formally denied this. The Chinese merchants, however, have long felt unable to bear the suffering of losses due to poor business conditions and have no ability to purchase, which is a fact. The reporter of Xin Sheng News Agency, after running around for several days and conducting investigations in various ways, learned that the exact number of the first batch of American cotton arriving in China was 58,000 bales, which were entrusted by the Chinese government to be sold by British and American merchants in Shanghai. Therefore, the rumor that it was purchased by Japanese merchants has now become a fact, that is, Tomen Co., Ltd. purchased 4,000 bales (Japanese weight) from the first batch of 58,000 bales of American cotton imported. The Japanese merchants concerned not only did not deny this news, but also said that the sales contract has been signed. Tomen Co., Ltd. attaches great importance to the purchase of this cotton because it has various political relations. Because of the deterioration of Anglo-Japanese relations and the resistance to Indian cotton, Japan's purchase of American cotton from our authorities is inevitable. It is also reported that the Chinese merchants held an emergency meeting a few days ago, advocating that half of the second batch of imported cotton should be sold by Chinese merchants. The total amount of Picimi cotton imported is as high as 4 million bales, of which 2.31 million bales are planned to be transported and sold to the interior. However, judging from the economic situation in the interior, it is feared that it is impossible, and it will eventually be resold to foreign merchants.

The Spread of the Communist Disaster in Sichuan Province 108

Telegraph to the Central Government 115

The Party Central Committee, the National Government Executive Yuan, the Judicial Yuan, and the Control Yuan are hereby informed that since the September 18th Incident, the people of the Northeast have been living in fear of national subjugation and have risen up to defend the country's territory. The righteous armies in various places have sprung up to resist the stubborn enemy in the north, and their will is firm. The righteous armies are commendable, and the people at home and abroad, in accordance with the principle of collective wisdom and strength, have enthusiastically contributed to the righteous cause, and there have been donations to support the righteous armies. Unexpectedly, at a time when the four provinces have been lost and the treaty has been signed under the city, there are people who are suspected of encroaching on and stealing donations from the public. What is more important than social credit, political prosperity, and the future of the nation? Moreover, according to another message, Guangzhou alone had remitted Ma only 73,700 yuan at that time. Taken together, the difference from the total amount of donations is more than 90%! The righteous armies shed blood at the national gate, which was the lifeline of the country at that time. Now, those who encroach on and steal donations are no different from criminals who destroy the country! The affiliated associations are all legitimate public groups, and they have the responsibility to investigate the funds donated by the public. Therefore, a joint committee has been jointly organized to engage in investigation matters. Although the investigation by public groups is only enough to express social indignation, social sanctions have not yet exerted the authority of national discipline and national law. Moreover, since they all belong to public groups, their powers are limited, and the effect is also limited. The way to remedy this is to rely on the country to exert its absolute authority and carry out judicial investigation, in addition to implementing social sanctions. Alas, the world is changing rapidly, and the national crisis has not ended. Strengthening national strength, defending oneself, and seeking survival depend on the collective wisdom and strength of the people. If even this lifeline of contributing to the righteous cause is cut off, then the destruction of social trust is also self-destruction of the nation's survival. If this is not investigated, and if the investigation is not thorough, can this nation that forgets the public for the sake of private gain still survive in this world? Therefore, we urge your office (departments) to order the Ministry of Judicial Administration to forward the order to the Procuratorate of the Shanghai Special Zone Court to conduct a thorough investigation as soon as possible in accordance with the meaning of the national prosecution. If there is no wrongdoing found, those who are public-minded, righteous, and self-respecting will be even more prominent. If there is wrongdoing found, those who are selfish and unlawful must be brought to justice and not allowed to escape, so that they can be warned and shown to the future. The prestige of the country and the future of the nation are truly dependent on this. We make this urgent plea and ask for your consideration.

Page 15

The Wenzhou Yangtong Fu Steamer Encountered Danger 120

Encountered Wind and Pirates, Engine Damaged by Water

Run Aground and Left Shoal Six Times

The Tong Fu merchant ship of the Tongan Company on Fuzhou Road in Shanghai encountered a sudden wind during its voyage from Pukou to Guangdong to transport coal. The engine was damaged, and the cabins were flooded, causing a major danger. It ran aground on the Wenzhou Ocean six times in a row. Now the ship's body is half-submerged in the Ou Sea. Shanghai has sent personnel to transport rescue pumpers to assist in the rescue. The details are divided and recorded as follows:

Encountered Wind at Dongting Lighthouse 121

The Tongan Company's Tong Fu ship, with a deadweight of 2,500 tons, loaded 3,300 tons of Zhongxing coal from Pukou on the 25th of last month to be delivered to Guangzhou. On the evening of the 26th, the ship passed Wusong. At 10:45 a.m. on the 27th, the ship arrived in Wenzhou waters and suddenly encountered a hurricane blowing from Hong Kong. Seeing that the situation was critical, the Tong Fu ship wanted to take shelter at the Dongting Lighthouse. However, the hurricane had already reached the stern. The Tong Fu's cabin was hit by huge wind and waves, causing damage to the engine in the engine room. It immediately chose a place to drop anchor and repair the engine. It took five hours before it could start sailing again.

Water Entered Near Bijia Mountain 122

It sailed out that night. At 5:45 a.m. on the 28th, water suddenly flooded into the engine room. The first mate flew to inform the captain. After testing for a long time, he could not find the source of the water entering the ship. The crew was very frightened and immediately used pumps to pump water. However, more water came in than was pumped out. At this point, the first mate asked the captain to quickly find an anchoring point to avoid accidents. At 9:40 a.m., he opened to Bijia Mountain, close to Pikishan, and dropped anchor and stopped sailing. Everyone was mobilized to repair the engine and worked hard to drain the water. However, the water in the ship was coming in very quickly, which was extremely dangerous at this time. The ship's body had a tendency to sink.

Wind阻海盜行劫 123

The Tong Fu ship originally had a radio, which was managed by radio operator Huang Zhonghao. This time, Huang suddenly left the ship and went ashore to resign to the company. The radio had been damaged and could not generate electricity, so after encountering the danger, it was unable to communicate with Shanghai for help at sea. It was delayed until 6:40 a.m. on the 29th before the captain changed direction and decided to sail to Wenzhou to avoid the danger of sinking. Just as he was about to raise the anchor and sail, at 12:40 p.m., a group of pirates suddenly arrived in a bandit ship to rob the Tong Fu, which had approached the outer block. The crew thought that this time they would be robbed by thieves and it would be difficult to escape. Unexpectedly, the sea was full of wind and waves, and the pirate ship was hit by the hurricane and could not get close to the Tong Fu. The shipowner [depending on the Secretary-General] took the opportunity to raise the anchor and fly away, and finally escaped. The ship arrived at Wenzhou Outer Port in the evening.

Ran Aground on Baishi Island 124

On the 30th, the water in the ship was still about six feet deep. The engine room was pumped first. At 3 p.m., the first mate said that it could be guaranteed to be safe, and then set off for Guangdong. It sailed for about three hours, and the water entering the engine room increased even more, exceeding six feet. The ship could hardly move, so it had to return to Wenzhou. At 9:50 p.m., when it arrived at White Rock outside Wenzhou, the ship ran aground. After an hour, it tried its best to knock down the car and retreat, and drove to Tiaolinggang to drop anchor. On the morning of the 31st, after being taken out of the water by a Jiangshang ship, Tong Fu ran aground again for the second time at 1:10 p.m. After various methods, it barely escaped the shoal at 3:10 p.m. and went to Wenzhou Zhonggang to wait for the tide.

Urgent Request for Assistance for the Stranded Ship 125

On August 1st, after the tide rose and the ship set sail, it ran aground for the third time just a few minutes later. It took another three hours to free it from the dangerous shoal. At 5 o'clock, it reached the waters off Laomiao but ran aground for the fourth time. The engine room was flooded with seawater, causing the ship to sink deeper and become unable to navigate. The Tongfu’s voyage to Wenzhou was a risky one, undertaken to prevent sinking. On the 2nd, at 10 o'clock, the ship used a 105-fathom-long cable to anchor in the deep water, waiting for the Ouhai Customs official, Han Lingjiang, to arrive and guide the ship. At 12 o'clock, it sailed at full speed, but unexpectedly ran aground again. It wasn't until 6:30 PM on the 3rd that the ship was finally freed from the shoal using maximum speed, but it had already been stranded for twenty-five hours. Finally, at 7:10 AM on the 4th, it entered Wenzhou Port, passed the first sandbar, and reached the Customs pier, where it anchored and urgently reported to the company, requesting assistance.

Shipowner Comes to Shanghai to Plead for Aid 126

The shipowner, relying on Slynsky, came to Shanghai because the ship's radio was damaged, and the engine room of the Tongfu ship was flooded, the source of the water unknown. Moreover, the bottom of the ship had suffered significant damage from running aground six times. The first priority was to pump out the water from the engine room, otherwise there was a risk of sinking. Therefore, he personally came to Shanghai to report to the company. The company's manager, Mr. Bao Anfu, personally went to Wenzhou to inspect. The result was that the Tongfu ship needed urgent rescue, otherwise the Oujiang sandbars were too numerous and the water shallow and dangerous, and an accident might occur, endangering the entire ship. So he immediately returned to Shanghai and dispatched a large number of technicians to Wenzhou to assist in the rescue.

Rescue Pump Transported to Wenzhou 127

The Tongfu ship's engine room was flooded, making it impossible to pump out the water. After Bao Anfu returned to Shanghai, he urgently rented a powerful rescue pump from Jardine Matheson, at a daily rental of 160 yuan. He also sent two specialized technicians and a group of workers, who have already taken the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haiyan ship to Wenzhou to use the pump to drain the water, so that the Tongfu ship can float to the surface. This time, the Tongfu ship first encountered a hurricane, then pirates, then the engine room flooded, and then it ran aground six times in a row. It is truly fortunate that it did not sink or get lost, but the various losses are very large.
